class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Civil parishes in Cornwall</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_civil_parishes_in_Cornwall&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="List of civil parishes in Cornwall">List of civil parishes in Cornwall</a>)</span></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornwall_UK_location_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="A map showing Cornwall and the Isles of Scilly, with major roads marked. Inset in top-left corner shows Cornwall within the UK" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Cornwall_UK_location_map.svg/250px-Cornwall_UK_location_map.svg.png" width="250" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Cornwall_UK_location_map.svg/375px-Cornwall_UK_location_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Cornwall_UK_location_map.svg/500px-Cornwall_UK_location_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="1048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornwall_UK_location_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Kernow</i>); the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Enesek Syllan</i>) are in the extreme bottom left</div></div></div>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Civil_parishes_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil parishes in England">civil parish</a> is a country subdivision, forming the lowest unit of <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_England" title="Local government in England">local government</a> in England. There are 218 civil parishes in the <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_county" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceremonial county">ceremonial county</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Kernow</i>), which includes the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>. The county is effectively parished in its entirety; only the unpopulated <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Rock,_Cornwall" class="mw-redirect" title="Wolf Rock, Cornwall">Wolf Rock</a> is unparished. At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">2001 census</a>, there were 501,267 people living in the current parishes, accounting for the whole of the county\'s population. The final unparished areas of mainland Cornwall, around <a href="/wiki/St_Austell" title="St Austell">St Austell</a>, were parished on 1 April 2009 to coincide with the <a href="/wiki/2009_structural_changes_to_local_government_in_England" title="2009 structural changes to local government in England">structural changes to local government in England</a>.\n</p><p>Population sizes within the county vary considerably, <a href="/wiki/Falmouth,_Cornwall" title="Falmouth, Cornwall">Falmouth</a> is the most populous with a population of 25,223, recorded in 2001, and <a href="/wiki/St_Michael%27s_Mount" title="St Michael&#39;s Mount">St Michael\'s Mount</a> the least with 29 residents. The county is governed by two separate <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authorities</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Council" title="Cornwall Council">Cornwall Council</a> covers mainland Cornwall and the Isles of Scilly are administered by their own unitary authority.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Civil_parishes_in_Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Parishes arose from <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> divisions, and were originally purely ecclesiastical. Over time they acquired civil administration powers.<sup id="cite_ref-anguswinchester_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anguswinchester-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Highways_Act_1555" title="Highways Act 1555">Highways Act 1555</a> made parishes responsible for the upkeep of roads. Every adult inhabitant of the parish was obliged to work four days a year on the roads, providing their own tools, carts and horses; the work was overseen by an unpaid local appointee, the <i>Surveyor of Highways</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The poor were looked after by the <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monasteries</a>, until their <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">dissolution</a>. In 1572, <a href="/wiki/Magistrates_of_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Magistrates of England and Wales">magistrates</a> were given power to \'survey the poor\' and impose taxes for their relief. This system was made more formal by the <a href="/wiki/Elizabethan_Poor_Law_(1601)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabethan Poor Law (1601)">Poor Law Act 1601</a>, which made parishes responsible for administering the <a href="/wiki/English_Poor_Laws" title="English Poor Laws">Poor Law</a>; overseers were appointed to charge a <a href="/wiki/Rates_(tax)" title="Rates (tax)">rate</a> to support the poor of the parish.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The 19th century saw an increase in the responsibility of parishes, although the <i>Poor Law</i> powers were transferred to <a href="/wiki/Poor_Law_Unions" class="mw-redirect" title="Poor Law Unions">Poor Law Unions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_district" title="Sanitary district">Public Health Act 1872</a> grouped parishes into Rural Sanitary Districts, based on the Poor Law Unions; these subsequently formed the basis for <a href="/wiki/Rural_district" title="Rural district">rural districts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Parishes were run by <a href="/wiki/Vestry" title="Vestry">vestries</a>, meeting annually to appoint officials, and were generally identical to ecclesiastical parishes,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> although some <a href="/wiki/Township_(England)" title="Township (England)">townships</a> in large parishes administered the <i>Poor Law</i> themselves. Under the <a href="/wiki/Divided_Parishes_and_Poor_Law_Amendment_Act_1882" title="Divided Parishes and Poor Law Amendment Act 1882">Divided Parishes and Poor Law Amendment Act 1882</a>, all <a href="/wiki/Extra-parochial_area" title="Extra-parochial area">extra-parochial areas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Township_(England)" title="Township (England)">townships</a> that levied a separate rate became independent civil parishes.<sup id="cite_ref-surname_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-surname-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Civil parishes in their modern sense date from the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1894" title="Local Government Act 1894">Local Government Act 1894</a>, which abolished vestries; established elected parish councils in all rural parishes with more than 300 electors; grouped rural parishes into Rural Districts; and aligned parish boundaries with county and borough boundaries.<sup id="cite_ref-surname_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-surname-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Urban civil parishes continued to exist, and were generally coterminous with the <a href="/wiki/Urban_district_(Great_Britain_and_Ireland)" title="Urban district (Great Britain and Ireland)">urban district</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipal_borough" title="Municipal borough">municipal borough</a> or <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> in which they were situated. Many large towns contained a number of parishes, and these were usually merged into one. Parish councils were not formed in urban areas, and the only function of the parish was to elect guardians to Poor Law Unions. With the abolition of the <i>Poor Law</i> system in 1930 the parishes had only a nominal existence.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government Act 1972</a> retained civil parishes in rural areas, and many former urban districts and municipal Boroughs that were being abolished, were replaced by new successor parishes. Urban areas that were considered too large to be single parishes became <a href="/wiki/Unparished_area" title="Unparished area">unparished areas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-act_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-act-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_position">Current position</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Civil_parishes_in_Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Current position">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Recent governments have encouraged the formation of town and parish councils in unparished areas. The <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_and_Rating_Act_1997" title="Local Government and Rating Act 1997">Local Government and Rating Act 1997</a> gave local residents the right to demand the creation of a new civil parish.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A parish council can become a town council unilaterally, simply by resolution. A civil parish can also gain <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status</a>, but only if that is granted by <a href="/wiki/British_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarchy">the Crown</a>. The chairman of a town or city council is called a <a href="/wiki/Mayors_in_England" title="Mayors in England">mayor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-act_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-act-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_and_Public_Involvement_in_Health_Act_2007" title="Local Government and Public Involvement in Health Act 2007">Local Government and Public Involvement in Health Act 2007</a> introduced alternative names: a parish council can now choose to be called a community; village; or neighbourhood council.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Within Cornwall, the 2007 Act lead to the abolition of the six <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_district" title="Non-metropolitan district">district councils</a> and Cornwall County Council, establishing in their place the single unitary authority, <a href="/wiki/Cornwall_Council" title="Cornwall Council">Cornwall Council</a>. All civil parish councils became the responsibility of this authority.<sup id="cite_ref-act_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-act-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> At the same time four new civil parishes were created in the <a href="/wiki/St_Austell_parishes" title="St Austell parishes">St Austell area</a>, parishing the last remaining populated part of the county.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCstAustell_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCstAustell-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="noviewer thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" href="/w/index.php?title=Civil_parishes_in_Cornwall&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<dl><dd><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Former_local_councilA"><a href="#ref_Former_local_councilA"><b><sup>A</sup></b></a></span> <small>From 1974 to 2009, mainland Cornwall was divided into districts: <a href="/wiki/Caradon" title="Caradon">Caradon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Karadon</i>), formed from Liskeard Municipal Borough, Liskeard Rural District, Looe Urban District, Saltash Municipal Borough, St Germans Rural District and Torpoint Urban District; <a href="/wiki/Carrick,_Cornwall" title="Carrick, Cornwall">Carrick</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Karrek</i>), formed from Falmouth Municipal Borough, Penryn Municipal Borough, Truro Municipal Borough and Truro Rural District; <a href="/wiki/Kerrier" title="Kerrier">Kerrier</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Keryer</i>), formed from Camborne\xe2\x80\x93Redruth Urban District, Helston Municipal Borough and Kerrier Rural District; <a href="/wiki/North_Cornwall" title="North Cornwall">North Cornwall</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Kernow Gledh</i>), formed from Bodmin Municipal Borough, Bude\xe2\x80\x93Stratton Urban District, Camelford Rural District, Launceston Municipal Borough, Launceston Rural District, Stratton Rural District and Wadebridge and Padstow Rural District; <a href="/wiki/Penwith" title="Penwith">Penwith</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Pennwydh</i>), formed from Penzance Municipal Borough, St Ives Municipal Borough, St Just Urban District and West Penwith Rural District; and <a href="/wiki/Restormel" title="Restormel">Restormel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>: <i lang="kw">Rostorrmoel</i>), formed from Newquay Urban District, St Austell Rural District and St Austell with Fowey Municipal Borough</small></dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
